	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Depression (mood)</h1>
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		<div id="contentSub2"></div>
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Hopelessness" redirects here. For the album by Anohni, see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hopelessness_(album)" title="Hopelessness (album)">Hopelessness (album)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Despair" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Despair_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Despair (disambiguation)">Despair (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">State of low mood and aversion to activity</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background:#ccc">Depression</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A man diagnosed as suffering from melancholia with strong su Wellcome L0026693.jpg" src="./depression_files/A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="319" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg/450px-A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg/600px-A_man_diagnosed_as_suffering_from_melancholia_with_strong_su_Wellcome_L0026693.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1101" data-file-height="1170"></a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithograph" class="mw-redirect" title="Lithograph">Lithograph</a> of a man diagnosed as suffering from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melancholia" title="Melancholia">melancholia</a> with strong suicidal tendency (1892)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Specialty_(medicine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Specialty (medicine)">Specialty</a></th><td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychiatry" title="Psychiatry">Psychiatry</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Depression</b> is a state of low <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_(psychology)" title="Mood (psychology)">mood</a> and aversion to activity. It can affect a person's thoughts, behavior, motivation, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeling" title="Feeling">feelings</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subjective_well-being" title="Subjective well-being">sense of well-being</a>. It may feature sadness, difficulty in thinking and concentration and a significant increase or decrease in appetite and time spent sleeping. People experiencing depression may have feelings of dejection, hopelessness and, sometimes, suicidal thoughts. It can either be short term or long term.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The core symptom of depression is said to be anhedonia, which refers to loss of interest or a loss of feeling of pleasure in certain activities that usually bring joy to people.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_2-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:1-2">[2]</a></sup> Depressed mood is a symptom of some <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_disorders" class="mw-redirect" title="Mood disorders">mood disorders</a> such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dysthymia" title="Dysthymia">dysthymia</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-DSM-5(2013)_3-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-DSM-5(2013)-3">[3]</a></sup> it is a normal temporary reaction to life events, such as the loss of a loved one; and it is also a symptom of some physical diseases and a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_effect" title="Side effect">side effect</a> of some drugs and medical treatments.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Factors">Factors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Factors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./depression_files/220px-Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="356" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg/330px-Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg/440px-Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2309" data-file-height="3737"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Allegory_on_Melancholy_Met_DP885774.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Allegory on melancholy, from circa 1729–40, etching and engraving, dimensions of the sheet: 42 × 25.7 cm, in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a> (New York City)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_events">Life events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Life events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Adversity in childhood, such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bereavement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bereavement">bereavement</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neglect" title="Neglect">neglect</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_abuse" class="mw-redirect" title="Mental abuse">mental abuse</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_abuse" title="Physical abuse">physical abuse</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a>, or unequal parental treatment of siblings can contribute to depression in adulthood.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Childhood physical or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexual abuse</a> in particular significantly correlates with the likelihood of experiencing depression over the victim's lifetime.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Life events and changes that may influence depressed moods include (but are not limited to): childbirth, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menopause" title="Menopause">menopause</a>, financial difficulties, unemployment, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychological_stress" title="Psychological stress">stress</a> (such as from work, education, family, living conditions etc.), a medical diagnosis (cancer, HIV, etc.), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a>, loss of a loved one, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_disaster" title="Natural disaster">natural disasters</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_isolation" title="Social isolation">social isolation</a>, rape, relationship troubles, jealousy, separation, or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catastrophic_injury" title="Catastrophic injury">catastrophic injury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">Adolescents</a> may be especially prone to experiencing a depressed <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">mood</a> following <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_rejection" title="Social rejection">social rejection</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer_pressure" title="Peer pressure">peer pressure</a>, or bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personality">Personality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Personality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Changes in personality or in one's social environment can affect levels of depression. High scores on the personality domain <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroticism" title="Neuroticism">neuroticism</a> make the development of depressive symptoms as well as all kinds of depression diagnoses more likely,<sup id="cite_ref-NeuroticismMA_11-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-NeuroticismMA-11">[11]</a></sup> and depression is associated with low <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extraversion" class="mw-redirect" title="Extraversion">extraversion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Other personality indicators could be: temporary but rapid mood changes, short term hopelessness, loss of interest in activities that used to be of a part of one's life, sleep disruption, withdrawal from previous social life, appetite changes, and difficulty concentrating.<sup id="cite_ref-healthline.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-healthline.com-13">[13]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_treatments">Medical treatments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Medical treatments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Depression may also be the result of healthcare, such as with medication induced depression. Therapies associated with depression include <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interferon" title="Interferon">interferon</a> therapy, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beta-blockers" class="mw-redirect" title="Beta-blockers">beta-blockers</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isotretinoin" title="Isotretinoin">isotretinoin</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contraceptives" class="mw-redirect" title="Contraceptives">contraceptives</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> cardiac agents, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anticonvulsants" class="mw-redirect" title="Anticonvulsants">anticonvulsants</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antimigraine_drug" title="Antimigraine drug">antimigraine drugs</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antipsychotics" class="mw-redirect" title="Antipsychotics">antipsychotics</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hormone_therapy" title="Hormone therapy">hormonal agents</a> such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonadotropin-releasing_hormone_agonist" title="Gonadotropin-releasing hormone agonist">gonadotropin-releasing hormone agonist</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Substance-induced">Substance-induced</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Substance-induced">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">drugs of abuse</a> can cause or exacerbate depression, whether in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Substance_intoxication" title="Substance intoxication">intoxication</a>, withdrawal, and from chronic use. These include <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedatives</a> (including prescription <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_disorder#Substance-induced" title="Mood disorder">benzodiazepines</a>), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opioid" title="Opioid">opioids</a> (including <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analgesic" title="Analgesic">prescription pain killers</a> and illicit drugs such as heroin), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stimulant" title="Stimulant">stimulants</a> (such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphetamines" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphetamines">amphetamines</a>), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hallucinogen" title="Hallucinogen">hallucinogens</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inhalants" class="mw-redirect" title="Inhalants">inhalants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:0-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-psychiatric_illnesses">Non-psychiatric illnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Non-psychiatric illnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(differential_diagnoses)" class="mw-redirect" title="Depression (differential diagnoses)">Depression (differential diagnoses)</a></div>
<p>Depressed mood can be the result of a number of infectious diseases, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nutritional_deficiency" class="mw-redirect" title="Nutritional deficiency">nutritional deficiencies</a>, neurological conditions,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and physiological problems, including <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypoandrogenism" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypoandrogenism">hypoandrogenism</a> (in men), <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Addison%27s_disease" title="Addison&#39;s disease">Addison's disease</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cushing%27s_syndrome" title="Cushing&#39;s syndrome">Cushing's syndrome</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypothyroidism" title="Hypothyroidism">hypothyroidism</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperparathyroidism" title="Hyperparathyroidism">hyperparathyroidism</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyme_disease" title="Lyme disease">Lyme disease</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parkinson%27s_disease" title="Parkinson&#39;s disease">Parkinson's disease</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chronic_pain" title="Chronic pain">chronic pain</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroke_recovery#Post-stroke_depression" title="Stroke recovery">stroke</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Saravane_18-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-Saravane-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychiatric_syndromes">Psychiatric syndromes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Psychiatric syndromes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_disorder#Depressive_disorders" title="Mood disorder">Depressive mood disorders</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="./depression_files/220px-Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="550" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png/330px-Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png/440px-Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="2000"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Depression-symptoms-and-early-warning-signs_orig.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Infographic</div></div></div>
<p>A number of psychiatric syndromes feature depressed mood as a main symptom. The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_disorder" title="Mood disorder">mood disorders</a> are a group of disorders considered to be primary disturbances of mood. These include <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a> (MDD; commonly called major depression or clinical depression) where a person has at least two weeks of depressed mood or a loss of interest or pleasure in nearly all activities; and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dysthymia" title="Dysthymia">dysthymia</a>, a state of chronic depressed mood, the symptoms of which do not meet the severity of a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_depressive_episode" title="Major depressive episode">major depressive episode</a>. Another mood disorder, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipolar_disorder" title="Bipolar disorder">bipolar disorder</a>, features one or more episodes of abnormally elevated mood, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition" title="Cognition">cognition</a>, and energy levels, but may also involve one or more episodes of depression.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> When the course of depressive episodes follows a seasonal pattern, the disorder (major depressive disorder, bipolar disorder, etc.) may be described as a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seasonal_affective_disorder" title="Seasonal affective disorder">seasonal affective disorder</a>.
Outside the mood disorders: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a> often features an extremely intense depressive mood; <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adjustment_disorder" title="Adjustment disorder">adjustment disorder with depressed mood</a> is a mood disturbance appearing as a psychological response to an identifiable event or stressor, in which the resulting emotional or behavioral symptoms are significant but do not meet the criteria for a major depressive episode;<sup id="cite_ref-psychiatric355_22-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-psychiatric355-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>355</span></sup> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Posttraumatic_stress_disorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Posttraumatic stress disorder">posttraumatic stress disorder</a>, a mental disorder that sometimes follows <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_trauma" title="Major trauma">trauma</a>, is commonly accompanied by depressed mood.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_legacy">Historical legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Historical legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dispossession,_oppression_and_depression" title="Dispossession, oppression and depression">Dispossession, oppression and depression</a></div>
<p>Researchers have begun to conceptualize ways in which the historical legacies of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonialism</a> may create depressive conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Measures">Measures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Measures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Measures of depression as an emotional disorder include, but are not limited to: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beck_Depression_Inventory" title="Beck Depression Inventory">Beck Depression Inventory-11</a> and the 9-item depression scale in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patient_Health_Questionnaire" title="Patient Health Questionnaire">Patient Health Questionnaire</a>. Both of these measures are psychological tests that ask personal questions of the participant, and have mostly been used to measure the severity of depression. The Beck Depression Inventory (BDI) is a self-report scale that helps a therapist identify the patterns of depression symptoms and monitor recovery. The responses on this scale can be discussed in therapy to devise interventions for the most distressing symptoms of depression.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_2-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:1-2">[2]</a></sup> Several studies, however, have used these measures to also determine healthy individuals who are not suffering from depression as a mental disorder, but as an occasional mood disorder. This is substantiated by the fact that depression as an emotional disorder displays similar symptoms to minimal depression and low levels of mental disorders such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_depressive_disorder" title="Major depressive disorder">major depressive disorder</a>; therefore, researchers were able to use the same measure interchangeably. In terms of the scale, participants scoring between 0-13 and 0-4 respectively were considered healthy individuals.<sup id="cite_ref-pmid29121529_26-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-pmid29121529-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>Another measure of depressed mood would be the IWP Multi-affect Indicator.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> It is a psychological test that indicates various emotions, such as enthusiasm and depression, and asks for the degree of the emotions that the participants have felt in the past week. There are studies that have used lesser items from the IWP Multi-affect Indicator which was then scaled down to daily levels to measure the daily levels of depression as an emotional disorder.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoprekstad_2019_28-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-Hoprekstad_2019-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Connections">Connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Alcoholism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alcohol can be a depressant which slows down some regions of the brain, like the prefrontal and temporal cortex, negatively affecting our rationality and memory.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> It also lowers the level of serotonin in our brain, which could potentially lead to higher chances of a depressive mood.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>The connection between the amount of alcohol intake, level of depressed mood, and how it affects the risks of experiencing consequences from alcoholism, were studied in a research done on college students. The study used 4 latent, distinct profiles of different alcohol intake and level of depression; Mild or Moderate Depression, and Heavy or Severe Drinkers. Other indicators consisting of social factors and individual behaviors were also taken into consideration in the research. Results showed that the level of depression as an emotion negatively affected the amount of risky behavior and consequence from drinking, while having an inverse relationship with protective behavioral strategies, which are behavioral actions taken by oneself for protection from the relative harm of alcohol intake. Having an elevated level of depressed mood does therefore lead to greater consequences from drinking.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bullying">Bullying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bullying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Social abuse, such as bullying, are defined as actions of singling out and causing harm on vulnerable individuals. In order to capture a day-to-day observation of the relationship between the damaging effects of social abuse, the victim's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_health" title="Mental health">mental health</a> and depressive mood, a study was conducted on whether individuals would have a higher level of depressed mood when exposed to daily acts of negative behavior. The result concluded that being exposed daily to abusive behaviors such as bullying has a positive relationship to depressed mood on the same day.
</p><p>The study has also gone beyond to compare the level of depressive mood between the victims and non-victims of the daily bullying. Although victims were predicted to have a higher level of depressive mood, the results have shown otherwise that exposure to negative acts has led to similar levels of depressive mood, regardless of the victim status. The results therefore have concluded that bystanders and non-victims feel as equally depressed as the victim when being exposed to acts such as social abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoprekstad_2019_28-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-Hoprekstad_2019-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Creative_thinking">Creative thinking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Creative thinking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Divergent thinking is defined as a thought process that generates creativity in ideas by exploring many possible solutions. Having a depressed mood will significantly reduce the possibility of divergent thinking, as it reduces the fluency, variety and the extent of originality of the possible ideas generated.<sup id="cite_ref-Mélendez_JC_2017_32-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-M%C3%A9lendez_JC_2017-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, some depressive mood disorders might have an positive effect for creativity. Upon identifying several studies and analyzing data involving individuals with high levels of creativity, Christa Taylor was able to conclude that there is a clear positive relationship between creativity and depressive mood. A possible reason is that having a low mood could lead to new ways of perceiving and learning from the world, but it is unable to account for certain depressive disorders. The direct relationship between creativity and depression remains unclear, but the research conducted on this correlation has shed light that individuals who are struggling with a depressive disorder may be having even higher levels of creativity than a control group, and would be a close topic to monitor depending on the future trends of how creativity will be perceived and demanded.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stress_management_techniques">Stress management techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stress management techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are empirical evidences of a connection between the type of stress management techniques and the level of daily depressive mood.<sup id="cite_ref-Mélendez_JC_2017_32-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-M%C3%A9lendez_JC_2017-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Problem-focused coping leads to lower level of depression. Focusing on the problem allows for the subjects to view the situation in an objective way, evaluating the severity of the threat in an unbiased way, thus it lowers the probability of having depressive responses. On the other hand, emotion-focused coping promotes a depressed mood in stressful situations. The person has been contaminated with too much irrelevant information and loses focus on the options for resolving the problem. They fail to consider the potential consequences and choose the option that minimizes stress and maximizes well-being.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Depressed mood may not require professional treatment, and may be a normal temporary reaction to life events, a symptom of some medical condition, or a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Side_effect" title="Side effect">side effect</a> of some drugs or medical treatments. A prolonged depressed mood, especially in combination with other symptoms, may lead to a diagnosis of a psychiatric or medical condition which may benefit from treatment. The UK <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Institute_for_Health_and_Care_Excellence" title="National Institute for Health and Care Excellence">National Institute for Health and Care Excellence</a> (NICE) 2009 guidelines indicate that <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">antidepressants</a> should not be routinely used for the initial treatment of <b>mild</b> depression, because the risk-benefit ratio is poor.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Physical activity can have a protective effect against the emergence of depression.<sup id="cite_ref-Sc2018_35-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-Sc2018-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>Physical activity can also decrease depressive symptoms due to the release of neurotrophic proteins in the brain that can help to rebuild the hippocampus that has been reduced due to depression.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Also <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoga" title="Yoga">yoga</a> could be considered an ancillary treatment option for patients with depressive disorders and individuals with elevated levels of depression.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>Reminiscence of old and fond memories is another alternative form of treatment, especially for the elderly who have lived longer and have more experiences in life. It is a method that causes a person to recollect memories of their own life, leading to a process of self-recognition and identifying familiar stimuli. By maintaining one's personal past and identity, it is a technique that stimulates people to view their lives in a more objective and balanced way, causing them to pay attention to positive information in their life stories, which would successfully reduce depressive mood levels.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Epidemiology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Depression is the leading cause of disability worldwide, the United Nations (UN) health agency reported, estimating that it affects more than 300 million people worldwide – the majority of them women, young people and the elderly. An estimated 4.4 per cent of the global population suffers from depression, according to a report released by the UN World Health Organization (WHO), which shows an 18 per cent increase in the number of people living with depression between 2005 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_Health_context_of_Depression">Global Health context of Depression</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Depression_(mood)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Global Health context of Depression">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Depression is major mental health cause of Global Burden of disease. Its consequences further lead to significant burden to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a>, which include higher risk of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a>, premature mortality arising from physical disorders and maternal depression impacts on child growth and development.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_43-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:2-43">[43]</a></sup>  Approximately 76% to 85% of depressed people in low and middle income countries  are not receiving treatments;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> barriers to treatment include: inaccurate assessment, lack of trained health care providers, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stigma" title="Social stigma">social stigma</a> and lack of resources.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_45-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:3-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> constructed guidelines aiming to increase services for people with mental, neurological and substance use disorders known as The Mental Health Gap Action Programme (mhGAP).<sup id="cite_ref-:3_45-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:3-45">[45]</a></sup> Depression is listed as one of conditions prioritized by the programme. Trials conducted show possibilities for the programme to be implemented on low-resource primary care settings dependent on primary care practitioners and lay health workers.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Examples of therapies by the mhGAP targeting depression are the Group Interpersonal Therapy as group treatment for depression and Thinking Health which utilizes <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_behavioral_therapy" title="Cognitive behavioral therapy">cognitive behavioral therapy</a> to tackle perinatal depression.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_45-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:3-45">[45]</a></sup> Furthermore, effective screening in primary care is crucial for the access of treatments. The mhGAP programme adopted its approach of improving detection rate of depression by training general practitioners. However, there is still weak evidence supporting this training.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_43-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood)#cite_note-:2-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
